With a ton of hay now fetching only $100, compared to $400 a couple of years ago, farmers are left with little choice but to consider alternative options [1].

The impact of drought on California's economy is further complicated by the state's progressive tax system, which makes it vulnerable to swings in the stock market [2]. If lawmakers and the governor get revenue projections wrong, the state may face a shortfall, and unlike the federal government, California is required to have a balanced budget [2]. Last year, the state's predictions were off due to a series of destructive storms that prompted lengthy delays in tax filing deadlines, resulting in a $42.9 billion lower revenue than estimated [2]. This highlights the challenges California faces in managing its finances during times of drought and economic

These examples illustrate the far-reaching consequences of drought and the need for effective water management policies to mitigate its effects.
